style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Sources: UK <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a> at <a href="/wiki/National_Air_Traffic_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="National Air Traffic Services">NATS</a><sup id="cite_ref-aip_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><br />Statistics from the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">UK Civil Aviation Authority</a><sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>London Southend Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>SEN</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EGMC</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> situated on the outskirts of <a href="/wiki/Southend-on-Sea" title="Southend-on-Sea">Southend-on-Sea</a> in <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>, England, approximately 36 miles (58&#160;km) from the <a href="/wiki/Charing_Cross#Official_use_as_central_point" title="Charing Cross">centre of London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The airport straddles the boundaries between the borough of <a href="/wiki/Southend-on-Sea" title="Southend-on-Sea">Southend-on-Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rochford_District" title="Rochford District">Rochford District</a>.\n</p><p>Southend was London\'s third-busiest airport from the 1960s until the end of the 1970s, when it was overtaken in passenger numbers by <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_Airport" title="London Stansted Airport">London Stansted Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-london110616_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-london110616-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ft110616_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft110616-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Following its purchase by <a href="/wiki/Stobart_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Stobart Group">Stobart Group</a> in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-ft110616_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft110616-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> a development programme<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc110404_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc110404-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> provided a new <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminal</a><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Control_tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Control tower">control tower</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc20110718_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20110718-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> extended <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runway</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and connection to <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">central London</a> via a regular rail service running between <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool Street Station">Liverpool Street Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southend_Airport_railway_station" title="Southend Airport railway station">Southend Airport Station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Shenfield%E2%80%93Southend_line" title="Shenfield\xe2\x80\x93Southend line">Shenfield\xe2\x80\x93Southend line</a>, continuing on to <a href="/wiki/Southend_Victoria" class="mw-redirect" title="Southend Victoria">Southend Victoria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc20110718_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20110718-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Early_years"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Early years</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#1993:_Regional_Airports_Ltd"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">1993: Regional Airports Ltd</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a flights</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#2020:_COVID-19_pandemic_and_consolidation"><span class="tocnumber">2.5</span> <span class="toctext">2020: COVID-19 pandemic and consolidation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Airlines_and_destinations"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Airlines and destinations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Statistics"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Statistics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Ground_transport"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Ground transport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Rail"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Rail</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Bus"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Bus</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Accidents_and_incidents"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Accidents and incidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Film_appearances"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Film appearances</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Description">Description</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Description">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport is located between <a href="/wiki/Southend-on-Sea" title="Southend-on-Sea">Southend-on-Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rochford" title="Rochford">Rochford</a> town centres, 1.5&#160;<a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">NM</a> (2.8&#160;km; 1.7&#160;mi) north of Southend,<sup id="cite_ref-aip_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> in the county of <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>, 36 miles (58&#160;km) east of central London. It has a single 1,856-metre (6,089&#160;ft) long asphalt runway on a south-west/north-east axis<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and is capable of handling passenger aircraft of <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a> and similar <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">wide-body aircraft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The current terminal was completed in February 2012. The terminal has since been extended by 90 metres, almost tripling the facility in size.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The former terminal now provides facilities for the handling of executive aircraft, with a business lounge and conference rooms.<sup id="cite_ref-New_Business_Lounge_for_high_flyers_opens_at_London_Southend_Airport_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Business_Lounge_for_high_flyers_opens_at_London_Southend_Airport-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A four-star <a href="/wiki/Holiday_Inn" title="Holiday Inn">Holiday Inn</a> hotel adjacent to the airport entrance, owned by the Stobart Group, opened on 1 October 2012, at that time having the only rooftop restaurant in Essex.<sup id="cite_ref-LondonSouthendAirport_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LondonSouthendAirport-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>London Southend was voted the best airport in Britain for three consecutive years by consumer group <i><a href="/wiki/Which%3F" title="Which?">Which?</a></i>, in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> 2014<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and again in 2015.,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and best London airport for 6 consecutive years 2013-2019<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Southend_airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Southend_airport.jpg/220px-Southend_airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Southend_airport.jpg/330px-Southend_airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Southend_airport.jpg/440px-Southend_airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2178" data-file-height="1158" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Southend_airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view looking north-east, prior to the construction of the runway extension</div></div></div>\n<p>Southend Airport handles mainly scheduled passenger, <a href="/wiki/Charter_flight" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter flight">charter</a>, cargo and <a href="/wiki/Air_charter" title="Air charter">business flights</a>, with some pilot training (both <a href="/wiki/Fixed-wing_aircraft" title="Fixed-wing aircraft">fixed-wing aircraft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">helicopter</a>) and private aircraft flying. The airport is run by London Southend Airport Co Ltd, which employs more than 150 people directly. Due to expansion, there were over 500 more people working at the airport in summer 2012 compared with summer 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Southend Airport has a <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">Civil Aviation Authority</a> (CAA) Ordinary Licence that allows flights for the public transport of passengers or for flying instruction as authorised by the licensee (London Southend Airport Company Limited).<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Southend Airport has an excellent weather record, and is used by airlines as a <a href="/wiki/Diversion_airport" title="Diversion airport">diversion alternative</a> when adverse weather or incidents cause other London airports to be closed.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airline ground handling is provided by the Stobart Group-owned Stobart Aviation Services,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> while the Stobart Jet Centre handles executive aircraft using the facility.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Companies located within the airport boundary employ more than 800 workers.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Previously <a href="/wiki/British_World_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="British World Airlines">British World Airlines</a> had its head office at Viscount House at London Southend Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a> began operating services by opening a base at Southend in April 2012<sup id="cite_ref-rail110617_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rail110617-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and Irish carrier <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus_Regional" title="Aer Lingus Regional">Aer Lingus Regional</a> began regular flights to Dublin in May,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> resulting in a rapid increase in airport passenger numbers during 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> with 721,661 using the airport in that year,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> 969,912 in 2013<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and 1,102,358 in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The following year saw a decline to 900,648 and again to 874,549 in 2016, while 2017 saw passenger numbers increase more than 25% to 1,095,914.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, the airport operator planned to reach passenger numbers of two million per year by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-london110616_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-london110616-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc110404_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc110404-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 2018 Southend Airport saw an increase of nearly 400,000 passengers over the previous year\'s total, with just over 1.4 million passengers using the airport, the highest annual total at the airport to that date.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airfield was established by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Flying_Corps" title="Royal Flying Corps">Royal Flying Corps</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. It was the largest flying ground in Essex, with the greatest number of units. In May 1915 the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_Air_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Navy Air Service">Royal Navy Air Service</a> (RNAS) took over until 4 June 1916, when it became RFC Rochford. It was designated as night fighter station and many sorties were flown against <a href="/wiki/Zeppelin" title="Zeppelin">Zeppelin</a> airship raiders, including LZ38 on 31 May 1915. Around 1919, the station closed and reverted to farmland, which it remained as until the 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airport was officially opened as a municipal airport on 18 September 1935 by the <a href="/wiki/Under-Secretary_of_State_for_Air" title="Under-Secretary of State for Air">Under-Secretary of State for Air</a>, Sir <a href="/wiki/Philip_Sassoon" title="Philip Sassoon">Philip Sassoon</a>, who arrived in his <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Leopard_Moth" title="De Havilland Leopard Moth">de Havilland Leopard Moth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1939, the <a href="/wiki/Air_Ministry" title="Air Ministry">Air Ministry</a> requisitioned the airfield and it was known as <i><a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">RAF</a> Rochford</i> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> as a satellite airfield. During World War II, it became a base for fighter squadrons comprising <a href="/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">Supermarine Spitfires</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Hurricane" title="Hawker Hurricane">Hawker Hurricanes</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Blenheim" title="Bristol Blenheim">Bristol Blenheims</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Many of the 50 <a href="/wiki/British_anti-invasion_preparations_of_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="British anti-invasion preparations of World War II">pillboxes</a> that were designed to protect the airport from <a href="/wiki/Paratrooper" title="Paratrooper">paratroop</a> landings still survive, as does the underground defence control room, which is near to Southend Flying Club. A further 20 or so pillboxes also remain in the surrounding countryside.\n<a href="/wiki/Canewdon" title="Canewdon">Canewdon</a>, 2 miles (3&#160;km) north-east of the airport, was the location of one of the World War II <a href="/wiki/Chain_Home" title="Chain Home">Chain Home</a> <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">radar</a> stations. The 360-foot (110&#160;m) high transmitter tower at Canewdon was relocated to the <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Company" title="Marconi Company">Marconi</a> works at <a href="/wiki/Great_Baddow" title="Great Baddow">Great Baddow</a> in the 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1993:_Regional_Airports_Ltd">1993: Regional Airports Ltd</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1993: Regional Airports Ltd">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barriers_on_road_by_Southend_Airport_(geograph_2074263).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Barriers_on_road_by_Southend_Airport_%28geograph_2074263%29.jpg/220px-Barriers_on_road_by_Southend_Airport_%28geograph_2074263%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Barriers_on_road_by_Southend_Airport_%28geograph_2074263%29.jpg/330px-Barriers_on_road_by_Southend_Airport_%28geograph_2074263%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Barriers_on_road_by_Southend_Airport_%28geograph_2074263%29.jpg/440px-Barriers_on_road_by_Southend_Airport_%28geograph_2074263%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barriers_on_road_by_Southend_Airport_(geograph_2074263).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Temporary closing of barriers across Eastwoodbury Lane was required for large aircraft movements until the road was diverted to enable the construction of the runway extension in August 2012</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1993, after the airport had been making losses for many years, Southend Borough Council sold the airport to Regional Airports Ltd (RAL), operator of <a href="/wiki/Biggin_Hill_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Biggin Hill Airport">Biggin Hill Airport</a>. London Southend Airport Co Ltd was formed to operate the airport which was re-branded as "London Southend Airport" with the term "Municipal" dropping from the title. The previous losses were turned into small profits for majority of tenure by RAL.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The largest aircraft ever to land at the Airport was in November 1998 when a <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_L-1011_Tristar" class="mw-redirect" title="Lockheed L-1011 Tristar">Lockheed L-1011 Tristar</a> of Irish airline <a href="/wiki/Aer_Turas" title="Aer Turas">Aer Turas</a> arrived for scrapping at the airport.\n</p><p>In 2001, a debate centred on the possible relocation of the <a href="/wiki/Categories_of_listed_building" class="mw-redirect" title="Categories of listed building">Grade I listed</a> <a href="/wiki/St._Laurence_and_All_Saints_Church,_Eastwood" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Laurence and All Saints Church, Eastwood">St Laurence and All Saints Church</a> further away from the side of the main runway. The proposal was dropped after the planning application was rejected by Southend Council in 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-engheritage_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-engheritage-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and a compromise scheme was implemented resulting in the installation of new barriers across Eastwoodbury Lane and requiring slightly shorter licensed runway lengths once safety areas had been added.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> These changes allowed passenger flights to be restarted, although the runway length still largely curtailed the potential range and payloads for passenger flights, and scheduled airline utilisation was low, until the March 2012 runway extension opened.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Flightline_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flightline (UK)">Flightline</a> was an airline formed in 1989 headquartered at Southend, where they also had a maintenance/engineering base for their own and third party aircraft. They mainly operated <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace_146" title="British Aerospace 146">British Aerospace 146</a> aircraft on ad-hoc charters, and an <a href="/wiki/BAe_146" class="mw-redirect" title="BAe 146">Avro RJ100</a> regional jet with which they operated a regular service between Southend and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> from 7 June 2006 to 1 December 2008 on behalf of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford Motor Company</a> as a corporate shuttle.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Flightline went into <a href="/wiki/Administration_(law)" title="Administration (law)">administration</a> on 3 December 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2008, Regional Airports Ltd put the airport up for sale.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> operated a once weekly summer-only service to Jersey using <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Dash_8" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier Dash 8">Dash 8</a> aircraft, ending in 2011.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008:_Stobart_Group">2008: Stobart Group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2008: Stobart Group">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Southend_Airport_railway_station_04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Southend_Airport_railway_station_04.jpg/220px-Southend_Airport_railway_station_04.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Southend_Airport_railway_station_04.jpg/330px-Southend_Airport_railway_station_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Southend_Airport_railway_station_04.jpg/440px-Southend_Airport_railway_station_04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Southend_Airport_railway_station_04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pre-extension terminal building seen from railway station, illustrating proximity.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Southend_Airport_terminal_building_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Southend_Airport_terminal_building_03.jpg/220px-Southend_Airport_terminal_building_03.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Southend_Airport_terminal_building_03.jpg/330px-Southend_Airport_terminal_building_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Southend_Airport_terminal_building_03.jpg/440px-Southend_Airport_terminal_building_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Southend_Airport_terminal_building_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of terminal building, seen from caf\xc3\xa9 by arrivals, and showing check-in area and escalator to departures.</div></div></div>\n<p>The airport was bought on 2 December 2008 by the <a href="/wiki/Stobart_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Stobart Group">Stobart Group</a> for <a href="/wiki/Pound_Sterling" class="mw-redirect" title="Pound Sterling">\xc2\xa3</a>21&#160;million, becoming part of the <a href="/wiki/Stobart_Air" title="Stobart Air">Stobart Air</a> division of the Stobart Group, which also operates <a href="/wiki/Carlisle_Lake_District_Airport" title="Carlisle Lake District Airport">Carlisle Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following council consultation with the local population, a planning application to extend the usable runway length by 300&#160;m (984&#160;ft) to 1,799&#160;m (5,902&#160;ft) and upgrade navigational and lighting aids, was submitted to <a href="/wiki/Southend_Borough_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Southend Borough Council">Southend Borough Council</a> 13 October 2009. Planning permission was granted 20 January 2010.\nInitially subject to an <a href="/wiki/Article_14_Direction" title="Article 14 Direction">Article 14 Direction</a>, after due consideration by the Government this was withdrawn 19 March 2010, meaning it would not be subject to a Public Inquiry.<sup id="cite_ref-SouthendEcho1_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SouthendEcho1-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Section_106_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Section 106 agreement">Section 106 agreement</a> was entered into between the airport and local councils.\n</p><p>On 1 June 2010, Stobart Group took a \xc2\xa3100&#160;million loan from M &amp; G Investments, partly in order to fund the airport construction.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In July 2010, an application for a <a href="/wiki/Judicial_review" title="Judicial review">judicial review</a> of the planning application was filed,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> which was dismissed on 2 February 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On 23 September 2010, the airport received the <i>Airport Achievement Award 2010/11</i> from the <a href="/wiki/European_Regions_Airline_Association" title="European Regions Airline Association">European Regions Airline Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A replacement <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">air traffic control</a> tower became operational 21 March 2011, followed by the return of year-round daily passenger services 27 March 2011 when <a href="/wiki/Aer_Arann" class="mw-redirect" title="Aer Arann">Aer Arann</a> commenced services to Galway and Waterford in Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a> announced a ten-year agreement with Stobart Group in June 2011, and in April 2012 commenced around 70 flights per week from Southend, using three <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319</a> aircraft based at the airport,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> flying to eight European destinations. <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">Easyjet\'s</a> operation at the airport has since increased to 16 destinations and in the summer of 2018 they will base a fourth aircraft at Southend, an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320">Airbus A320</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A new on-site <a href="/wiki/Southend_Airport_railway_station" title="Southend Airport railway station">rail station</a> opened on 18 July 2011, (the official opening by Minister for Transport <a href="/wiki/Theresa_Villiers" title="Theresa Villiers">Theresa Villiers</a> MP was on 21 September 2011),<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and a new road opened on 1 September 2011, replacing Eastwoodbury Lane that lay in the path required for the runway extension.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012-2019:_London_Olympics_and_expansion_of_passenger_flights">2012-2019: London Olympics and expansion of passenger flights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2012-2019: London Olympics and expansion of passenger flights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympic_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 Summer Olympic Games">2012 Summer Olympic Games</a>, a new terminal was built by Buckingham Group Contracting Ltd during 2011 and opened 28 February 2012 (the official opening was by Justine Greening, Secretary of State for Transport, on 5 March 2012).<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The original terminal has been redeveloped for use by private jets, with <a href="/wiki/Stobart_Air" title="Stobart Air">Stobart Air</a> having invested half a million pounds turning it into an executive business lounge.<sup id="cite_ref-London_Southend_Airport_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_Southend_Airport-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The extended runway opened on 8 March 2012, with Category I ILS on both ends of the runway.\n</p><p>In spring 2014, <a href="/wiki/Stobart_Air" title="Stobart Air">Stobart Air</a> announced that it had agreed a five-year <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchise agreement</a> with <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> which would see two Flybe-branded aircraft based at Southend operating six routes from summer 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> On 18 January 2015, two routes were terminated with the operation reduced to one aircraft. On 7 April 2014, the extension to the passenger terminal was formally opened by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_McLoughlin" title="Patrick McLoughlin">Patrick McLoughlin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Transport" title="Secretary of State for Transport">Secretary of State for Transport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>ATC Lasham, the major engineering company at the airport, entered administration in October 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The main <a href="/wiki/Hangar" title="Hangar">hangar</a> that it used dated back to <a href="/wiki/Aviation_Traders" title="Aviation Traders">Aviation Traders Engineering Limited</a> (ATEL) \xe2\x80\x93 founded by the late Sir <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Laker" title="Freddie Laker">Freddie Laker</a> \xe2\x80\x93 and was later used by Heavylift Engineering.\n</p><p>In December 2016, Flybe announced it would be adding new routes from summer 2017 to 12 European destinations, primarily aimed at the weekend break customers.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The airline based two <a href="/wiki/Embraer_E-Jet_family" title="Embraer E-Jet family">Embraer 195</a> aircraft at the airport.\nIn October 2017, <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> added high frequency domestic routes to the airport, with up to 18 flights per week to <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, up to 16 flights per week to <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> and up to 10 flights per week to <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>. An additional ATR 72 was based at the airport to operate the Manchester flights, bringing the total number of Flybe aircraft based at Southend to four.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2018, <a href="/wiki/Air_Malta" title="Air Malta">Air Malta</a> announced it would begin flights to <a href="/wiki/Cagliari" title="Cagliari">Cagliari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catania" title="Catania">Catania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> which began in May 2018 although the <a href="/wiki/Cagliari" title="Cagliari">Cagliari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catania" title="Catania">Catania</a> flights ceased in January 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\nIn June 2018, <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> announced it would open a base at Southend, basing three aircraft there operating 55 flights per week to 13 destinations,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> which began in April 2019.\nIn October 2018, <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> announced it would commence 5 flights per week to <a href="/wiki/Newquay_Airport" title="Newquay Airport">Newquay Airport</a> from April 2019, increasing to daily from May 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2019 <a href="/wiki/Loganair" title="Loganair">Loganair</a> started to fly to <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stornoway" title="Stornoway">Stornoway</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> in July 2019 to <a href="/wiki/Carlisle_Lake_District_Airport" title="Carlisle Lake District Airport">Carlisle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/City_of_Derry_Airport" title="City of Derry Airport">Derry</a> flights moved from <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Stansted airport">Stansted</a> to Southend on 27 October 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 31 October 2019 Ryanair announced four new routes to launch in Summer 2020 - Bergerac, Girona and Marseille<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> were first announced before Rodez was announced<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> as the route was moved from Stansted to Southend.\nOn 14 November 2019 Loganair announced that the Stornoway to Glasgow to Southend service would be withdrawn from 3 January 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2020:_COVID-19_pandemic_and_consolidation">2020: COVID-19 pandemic and consolidation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2020: COVID-19 pandemic and consolidation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 22 January 2020, Norwegian airline <a href="/wiki/Wider%C3%B8e" title="Wider\xc3\xb8e">Wider\xc3\xb8e</a> announced it would move its Kristiansand route from Stansted to Southend at the start of the Summer 2020 season,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> however due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="COVID-19 pandemic in the United Kingdom">COVID-19</a> pandemic this has now been postponed until 26 October 2020. On 20 February 2020, it was announced Loganair would suspend its Aberdeen service<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> and on 23 March, similarly the Carlisle service.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> At the commencement of the COVID-19 UK lockdown, <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a>\'s revised schedule consolidated the <a href="/wiki/Sibiu" title="Sibiu">Sibiu</a> route at <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">London Luton Airport</a> from when it re-started, cutting the route from Southend. In June 2020, Wizz Air cut <a href="/wiki/Vilnius" title="Vilnius">Vilnius</a> as a destination from Southend as well,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> leaving it with one route to <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>.\n</p><p>On 17 August 2020, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> announced it would close its base at Southend entirely due to the coronavirus pandemic, the last scheduled flight occurring on 31 August 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled and charter flights at London Southend Airport:<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th class="unsortable">Destinations</th></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Alicante%E2%80%93Elche_Airport" title="Alicante\xe2\x80\x93Elche Airport">Alicante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henri_Coand%C4%83_International_Airport" title="Henri Coand\xc4\x83 International Airport">Bucharest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faro_Airport" title="Faro Airport">Faro</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_Airport" title="M\xc3\xa1laga Airport">M\xc3\xa1laga</a> <br /><b>Seasonal:</b> <a href="/wiki/Orio_al_Serio_International_Airport" title="Orio al Serio International Airport">Bergamo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilbao_Airport" title="Bilbao Airport">Bilbao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brest_Bretagne_Airport" title="Brest Bretagne Airport">Brest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corfu_International_Airport" title="Corfu International Airport">Corfu</a>, <a title="Vilnius Airport">Vilnius</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Henri_Coand%C4%83_International_Airport" title="Henri Coand\xc4\x83 International Airport">Bucharest</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1017906329">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output mw-graph-nofallback" style="min-width:540px;min-height:300px" data-graph-id="89c16fa8818c23240d83684558098908a1d236a5"></div>\n<p><small>See <a class="external text" class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transport">Ground transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ground transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Southend_Airport_railway_station_(geograph_2515721).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Southend_Airport_railway_station_%28geograph_2515721%29.jpg/220px-Southend_Airport_railway_station_%28geograph_2515721%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Southend_Airport_railway_station_%28geograph_2515721%29.jpg/330px-Southend_Airport_railway_station_%28geograph_2515721%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Southend_Airport_railway_station_%28geograph_2515721%29.jpg/440px-Southend_Airport_railway_station_%28geograph_2515721%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="467" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Southend_Airport_railway_station_(geograph_2515721).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Southend_Airport_railway_station" title="Southend Airport railway station">Southend Airport railway station</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since 2011, the airport has its own railway station near the terminal building, <a href="/wiki/Southend_Airport_railway_station" title="Southend Airport railway station">Southend Airport railway station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Shenfield_to_Southend_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Shenfield to Southend Line">Shenfield to Southend Line</a>, which is served by <a href="/wiki/Abellio_Greater_Anglia" class="mw-redirect" title="Abellio Greater Anglia">Abellio Greater Anglia</a> connecting the airport to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">Liverpool Street station</a> in London up to eight times per hour during peak times and <a href="/wiki/Southend_Victoria_railway_station" title="Southend Victoria railway station">Southend Victoria railway station</a> in the other direction respectively. The journey to London takes about 55 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A later train has now been added to London every night, except Saturday night, and an earlier train to the airport from London every day, except Sunday morning.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport is served by buses operated by <a href="/wiki/Arriva_Southend" title="Arriva Southend">Arriva Southend</a> from the airport entrance to <a href="/wiki/Southend" class="mw-redirect" title="Southend">Southend</a> (7, 8 and 9), <a href="/wiki/Rochford" title="Rochford">Rochford</a> (7 and 8), <a href="/wiki/Ashingdon" title="Ashingdon">Ashingdon</a> (7), <a href="/wiki/Hawkwell" title="Hawkwell">Hawkwell</a> (8), <a href="/wiki/Hockley" title="Hockley">Hockley</a> (7 and 8), <a href="/wiki/Eastwood,_Essex" title="Eastwood, Essex">Eastwood</a> (9) and <a href="/wiki/Rayleigh,_Essex" title="Rayleigh, Essex">Rayleigh</a> (7, 8 and 9).<sup id="cite_ref-Arriva_Southend_Routes_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arriva_Southend_Routes-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/First_Essex" title="First Essex">First Essex</a> operates <a href="/wiki/Essex_Airlink" title="Essex Airlink">Essex Airlink X30</a> from the terminal to <a href="/wiki/Chelmsford" title="Chelmsford">Chelmsford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Stansted Airport">Stansted Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-X30_Timetable_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-X30_Timetable-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Since 5 October 2019, <a href="/wiki/Ensignbus" title="Ensignbus">Ensignbus</a> have operated the Jetlink X1, a night bus service running once in each direction from Southend Airport to <a href="/wiki/Grosvenor_Gardens,_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Grosvenor Gardens, London">Grosvenor Gardens, London</a> via <a href="/wiki/Lakeside_Shopping_Centre" title="Lakeside Shopping Centre">Lakeside Shopping Centre</a> bus station, <a href="/wiki/Canning_Town_bus_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Canning Town bus station">Canning Town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Embankment_tube_station" title="Embankment tube station">Embankment</a> stations.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>On 11 February 1944, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_B-17_Flying_Fortress" title="Boeing B-17 Flying Fortress">Boeing B-17</a> 42-31694 of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">USAAF</a> (511th BS) crash-landed and burned out at Southend, after receiving battle damage on a raid on <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 11 May 1944, B17G 42-107147 of the USAAF (360BS) made an <a href="/wiki/Emergency_landing" title="Emergency landing">emergency</a> <a href="/wiki/Belly_landing" title="Belly landing">wheels-up</a> landing with heavy <a href="/wiki/Flak" class="mw-redirect" title="Flak">flak</a> damage after a mission to <a href="/wiki/Saarbr%C3%BCcken" title="Saarbr\xc3\xbccken">Saarbr\xc3\xbccken</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 12 July 1957, a <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Constellation" title="Lockheed Constellation">Lockheed Constellation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">TWA</a> made an <a href="/wiki/Emergency_landing" title="Emergency landing">emergency landing</a> while routeing from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt</a> to <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a>, with one engine on fire.<sup id="cite_ref-SoutheastMissourianpage2,7thcolumn_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SoutheastMissourianpage2,7thcolumn-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 28 July 1959, an East Anglian Flying Services <a href="/wiki/Vickers_VC.1_Viking" title="Vickers VC.1 Viking">Vickers 614 Viking 1</a> (<a href="/wiki/Aircraft_registration" title="Aircraft registration">registered</a> G-AHPH) was written off in a landing accident. On <a href="/wiki/Final_approach_(aviation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Final approach (aviation)">approach</a> the aircraft\'s right-hand main gear indicator showed that the gear was unsafe. An <a href="/wiki/Emergency_landing" title="Emergency landing">emergency landing</a> was made on the grass parallel to the runway. The right gear collapsed and the aircraft swung to the right, damaging it beyond repair. None of the 39 occupants were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 9 October 1960, a <a href="/wiki/Handley_Page_Hermes" title="Handley Page Hermes">Handley Page Hermes</a> of <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Airways" title="Falcon Airways">Falcon Airways</a> (registration: G-ALDC) overran the runway on landing, ending up across the <a href="/wiki/Shenfield_to_Southend_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Shenfield to Southend Line">Shenfield to Southend</a> railway line. The aircraft was written off but all 76 people on board survived.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN091060_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN091060-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 3 May 1967, a <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> of <a href="/wiki/Channel_Airways" title="Channel Airways">Channel Airways</a> (registration: G-AVJZ) was written off when a propeller was feathered on take-off. Two people on the ground died.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN030567_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN030567-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 4 May 1968, a <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> of <a href="/wiki/Channel_Airways#Accidents_and_incidents" title="Channel Airways">Channel Airways</a> (registration: G-APPU) overran the runway having landed at too high a speed. The aircraft was written off.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN040568_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN040568-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 3 June 1971, a <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">Douglas DC-3</a> of Moormanair (registration: PH-MOA) returned for an emergency landing with one engine partially failed, shortly after departure to the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> carrying supporters of <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax Football Club</a>. It overran on landing, colliding with an earth bank at the end of the runway and slightly injuring 2 of the 32 passengers on board.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN030671_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN030671-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AIB173_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIB173-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 4 October 1974, the <a href="/wiki/Flight_engineer" title="Flight engineer">flight engineer</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Transport" title="Delta Air Transport">DAT</a> <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-6" title="Douglas DC-6">Douglas DC-6</a> (registration: OO-VGB) retracted the nose gear during take-off, even though the aircraft was not yet airborne, due to a communication error with the pilots. The aircraft slid along the runway and was damaged beyond repair. Of the 99 passengers on board the flight to Antwerp, one was severely injured and another four received minor injuries from evacuating the aircraft. The six crew members remained uninjured.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 9 March 1986, a <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> (registration: G-BLNB) made a wheels up landing, the landing gear warning horn not having functioned correctly. There were no injuries to the 3 occupants; after repair the aircraft was returned to service.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 12 September 1987, a <a href="/wiki/Beechcraft_200" class="mw-redirect" title="Beechcraft 200">Beechcraft 200</a> (registration: G-WSJE) carrying newspapers crash landed at night into Mac\'s Garage on the Eastwood Road. The pilot, 33-year-old Hugh Forrester Brown from nearby <a href="/wiki/Canewdon" title="Canewdon">Canewdon</a>, was thought to have attempted to crash land on the road after take-off, but was unable to and crashed into the uninhabited garage.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 11 January 1988, a <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> of <a href="/wiki/British_United_Air_Ferries#Accidents_and_incidents" title="British United Air Ferries">British Air Ferries</a> (registration: G-APIM) was damaged beyond economic repair when it was in a ground collision with a Fairflight <a href="/wiki/Short_330" title="Short 330">Short 330</a> (registration: G-BHWT). The BAF <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Viscount</a> was subsequently repaired and donated to <a href="/wiki/Brooklands_Museum" title="Brooklands Museum">Brooklands Museum</a> for preservation.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN110188_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN110188-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 6 March 1997, a <a href="/wiki/Piper_PA-34_Seneca" title="Piper PA-34 Seneca">Piper PA-34 Seneca</a> (registration: G-NJML) flying a charter taking aircraft spare parts to <a href="/wiki/Ostend" title="Ostend">Ostend</a>, crashed 3.5 miles (5.6&#160;km) to the north-east of the airport while attempting to return following the failure of the <a href="/wiki/Gyroscope" title="Gyroscope">gyroscope</a> in the aircraft\'s <a href="/wiki/Attitude_indicator" title="Attitude indicator">attitude indicator</a>. One of the two occupants died, the other seriously injured.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 19 July 2006, a <a href="/wiki/Cessna_150" title="Cessna 150">Cessna 150</a> (registration: G-BABB) being flown by a student pilot on his second solo flight crashed into a public park 1&#160;nmi (1.9&#160;km; 1.2&#160;mi) from the airport. The student pilot was fatally injured.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_appearances">Film appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Southend_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Film appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>A <a href="/wiki/British_United_Air_Ferries" title="British United Air Ferries">British United Air Ferries</a> Carvair is seen transporting <a href="/wiki/Auric_Goldfinger" title="Auric Goldfinger">Auric Goldfinger</a> and his car in the 1964 <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Goldfinger_(film)" title="Goldfinger (film)">Goldfinger</a></i> from Southend Airport to <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>. In the scene, filmed in 1963, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Connery" title="Sean Connery">Sean Connery</a> as Bond drives his <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin_DB5" title="Aston Martin DB5">Aston Martin DB5</a> into Southend Airport (having tracked Goldfinger\'s Rolls Royce to the airport), and takes it to Switzerland in pursuit of Goldfinger via the <a href="/wiki/Carvair" class="mw-redirect" title="Carvair">Carvair</a> service.</li>\n<li>The airport also appears in the 2001 film <i><a href="/wiki/Mike_Bassett:_England_Manager" title="Mike Bassett: England Manager">Mike Bassett: England Manager</a></i>. It is shown when the team emerge to joyous crowds upon their arrival from the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> in Brazil.</li></ul>\n<h2><span
